     <p><b>McGill University</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. Founded in 1821 during the <a href="/wiki/Canada_under_British_Imperial_Control_(1764-1867)" title="Canada under British Imperial Control (1764-1867)" class="mw-redirect">British colonial era</a>, the university bears the name of <a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, a prominent Montreal merchant from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and alumnus of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_University" title="Glasgow University" class="mw-redirect">Glasgow University</a>, whose bequest formed the beginning of the university. Several colleges and universities were established by McGill, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">University of British Columbia</a>, which was known as the McGill University College of British Columbia until 1915, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">University of Victoria</a>, an affiliated junior college of McGill until 1916, and <a href="/wiki/Dawson_College" title="Dawson College">Dawson College</a> which began in 1945 as a satellite campus of McGill to absorb the anticipated influx of students after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. In addition, McGill medical graduate and former professor, <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, was among the four founders and early faculty members of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins School of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Both founders of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>, Premier <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Cameron_Rutherford" title="Alexander Cameron Rutherford">Alexander Cameron Rutherford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a>, were also McGill alumni.</p> 
     <p>With almost 215,000 living alumni worldwide, students and professors at McGill have been recognized in fields ranging from the arts and sciences, to business, politics, diplomacy, and sports. Notable alumni include nine <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel Laureates</a> (overall, twelve <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation#Other_universities" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel laureates</a> are affiliated with the university), one hundred and thirty-four <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a> (more than any other Canadian university),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> three astronauts, two <a href="/wiki/Canadian_prime_ministers" title="Canadian prime ministers" class="mw-redirect">Canadian prime ministers</a>, twelve justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Canadian Supreme Court</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> four <a href="/wiki/Leader" title="Leader" class="mw-redirect">foreign leaders</a>, twenty-eight foreign ambassadors, nine <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners, three <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners, and twenty-eight <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medalists. In addition, McGill alumni were instrumental in inventing or initially organizing <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lennox2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lennox2009-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill University is one of two member-universities of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> situated outside the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of the 2012-2013 school year, McGill was ranked 1st in Canada among all its major/research universities offering medical and doctoral degrees in the <a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a> 22nd annual rankings, maintaining this position for the eighth consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Internationally, McGill ranked 18th in the world and 1st in Canada in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>'s Top 400 Universities,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> maintaining its ranking among the top 20 universities globally, and as Canada's top university, for the ninth consecutive year. <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_BusinessWeek" title="Bloomberg BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">Bloomberg BusinessWeek</a>'s 2012 Business Schools Ranking ranked McGill's Desautels Faculty of Management 10th in the world among non-US business schools, referring to McGill University as &quot;the #1 university in Canada and among the top 20 worldwide.&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill was ranked 34th in the world and 3rd in Canada by the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>,.<sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 Emerging/Trendence Global Employability Ranking, McGill was ranked 19th in the world, and 1st in Canada, for popularity among major employers.<sup id="cite_ref-NYtimes_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYtimes-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">Travel + Leisure</a> rated McGill's campus as one of the 17 most beautiful university campuses in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The main campus is set upon 32 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> (79&nbsp;acres) at the foot of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Montreal" title="Downtown Montreal">Downtown Montreal</a>, covering much of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Square_Mile" title="Golden Square Mile">Golden Square Mile</a>. A second campus, the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a>, is situated on 6.5 square kilometres (1,600 acres) of fields and forested land in <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue,_Quebec" title="Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, Quebec">Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue</a>, 30&nbsp;km (19&nbsp;mi) west of the downtown campus. With 21 <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(university)" title="Faculty (university)" class="mw-redirect">faculties</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_schools" title="Professional schools" class="mw-redirect">professional schools</a>, McGill offers degrees and diplomas in over 300 fields of study, including medicine and law. Although the language of instruction is <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">English</a>, students have the right to submit any graded work in English or in French, except when learning a particular language is an objective of the course. Approximately 38,000 students attend McGill, with international students comprising one-fifth of the student population.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Institution_for_the_Advancement_of_Learning">Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The creation of the Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning (RIAL) in 1801, and its formation of two new Royal Grammar Schools in 1816, acted as turning points for Canada in two particular ways. First, the schools &quot;were created by legislation, the District Public Schools Act of 1807, and they showed the government's willingness to support the costs of education and even the salary of a schoolmaster. Second, the law involved the state in education, an important first step in the creation of nondenominational schools.&quot; The original two schools closed in 1846; by the mid-19th century the RIAL lost control of the other 82 <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools" title="Grammar schools" class="mw-redirect">grammar schools</a> it had administered.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Its sole remaining purpose was to administer the McGill bequests on behalf of the college. McGill College continued to grow, now having the sole aim of providing <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">post-secondary education</a>. The RIAL continues to exist today; it is the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a> that runs the university and its various constituent bodies, including the former Macdonald College (now Macdonald Campus), the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Institute" title="Montreal Neurological Institute" class="mw-redirect">Montreal Neurological Institute</a> and the Royal Victoria College (the former women's college turned residence). Since the revised Royal Charter of 1852, The Trustees of the RIAL comprise the Board of Governors of McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McGill_College">McGill College</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: McGill College">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:James_McGill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/170px-James_McGill.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/255px-James_McGill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/340px-James_McGill.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:James_McGill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, the original 
        <a href="/wiki/Benefactor_(law)" title="Benefactor (law)">benefactor</a> of McGill University.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, Scotland on 6 October 1744, was a successful English and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French-speaking</a> merchant in Quebec, having matriculated into <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">Glasgow University</a> in 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Between 1811 and 1813<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> he drew up a will leaving his &quot;Burnside estate&quot;, a 19-hectare (47-acre) tract of <a href="/wiki/Rural" title="Rural" class="mw-redirect">rural</a> land and 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pounds</a> to the Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kip_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kip-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Upon McGill's death in December 1813, the Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning, established in 1801 by an Act of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Lower_Canada" title="Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada">Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-charter_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> added the establishing of a University pursuant to the conditions of McGill's will to its original function of administering <a href="/wiki/Elementary_education" title="Elementary education" class="mw-redirect">elementary education</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a>. As a condition of the bequest, the land and funds had to be used for the establishment of a &quot;University or College, for the purposes of Education and the Advancement of Learning in the said Province.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-charter_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The will specified that a constituent college would be required to bear his name and the school must be established within 10 years of his death; otherwise the bequest would revert to the heirs of his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On March 31, 1821, after protracted <a href="/wiki/Legal_battle" title="Legal battle" class="mw-redirect">legal battles</a> with the Desrivieres family (the heirs of his wife), McGill College received a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> from <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">King George IV</a>. The Charter provided that the College should be deemed and taken as a <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">University</a>, with the power of conferring <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degrees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/220px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/330px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/440px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Arts Building, completed in 1843 and designed by 
        <a href="/wiki/John_Ostell" title="John Ostell">John Ostell</a>, is the oldest building on campus still standing.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Despite having a royal charter, McGill College was inactive until 1829 when the Montreal Medical Institution, which had been founded in 1823, became the college's first academic unit and Canada's first medical school. The Faculty of Medicine granted its first degree, a Doctor of Medicine and Surgery, in 1833; this was also the first medical degree to be awarded in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculty of Medicine remained the school's only functioning faculty until 1843 when the Faculty of Arts commenced teaching in the newly constructed Arts Building and East Wing (Dawson Hall).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also historically has strong linkage with the <a href="/wiki/The_Canadian_Grenadier_Guards" title="The Canadian Grenadier Guards">The Canadian Grenadier Guards</a>, a military regiment in which James McGill served as the Lieutenant-Colonel. This title is marked upon the stone that stands before the Arts building, from where the Guards step off annually to commemorate Remembrance Day.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_development">Later development</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Later development">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JohnWilliamDawson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JohnWilliamDawson.jpg/170px-JohnWilliamDawson.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/JohnWilliamDawson.jpg/255px-JohnWilliamDawson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/58/JohnWilliamDawson.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JohnWilliamDawson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Sir John William Dawson, Principal of McGill University 1855-1893.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/John_William_Dawson" title="John William Dawson">Sir John William Dawson</a>, McGill's principal from 1855 to 1893, is often credited with transforming the school into a modern university.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> He recruited the aid of Montreal's wealthiest citizens (eighty percent of Canada's wealth was then controlled by families who lived within the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Square_Mile" title="Golden Square Mile">Golden Square Mile</a> area that surrounded the university), many of whom donated property and funding needed to construct the campus buildings. Their names adorn many of the campus's prominent buildings. William Spier (architect) designed the addition of West Wing of the Arts Building for William Molson, 1861.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Francis_Dunlop" title="Alexander Francis Dunlop">Alexander Francis Dunlop</a> designed major alterations to the East Wing of McGill College (now called the Arts Building, MCGill University) for Prof. Bovey and the Science Dept., 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> This expansion of the campus continued until 1920. Buildings designed by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Taylor_(Architect)" title="Andrew Taylor (Architect)" class="mw-redirect">Andrew Taylor (Architect)</a>, include the <a href="/wiki/Redpath_Museum" title="Redpath Museum">Redpath Museum</a> (1880), Macdonald Physics Building (1893), the Redpath Library (1893), the Macdonald Chemistry Building (1896), the Macdonald Engineering Building (1907), and the Strathcona Medical Building (1907)—since renamed the Strathcona Anatomy and Dentistry Building.</p> 
     <p>In 1885, the university's Board of Governors formally adopted the use of the name McGill University. The Faculty of Law was founded in 1848, making it Canada's oldest. The school of architecture at McGill University was founded in 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Women's education at McGill began in 1884, when <a href="/wiki/Donald_Smith,_1st_Baron_Strathcona_and_Mount_Royal" title="Donald Smith, 1st Baron Strathcona and Mount Royal">Donald Smith</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/Lord_Strathcona" title="Lord Strathcona" class="mw-redirect">Lord Strathcona</a>, began funding separate lectures for women, given by university staff members. The first degrees granted to women at McGill were conferred in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1899, the Royal Victoria College (RVC) opened as a residential college for women at McGill. Until the 1970s, all female undergraduate students, known as &quot;Donaldas,&quot; were considered to be members of RVC.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in the autumn of 2010, the newer Tower section of Royal Victoria College is a <i>co-ed</i> dormitory, whereas the older West Wing remains strictly for women. Both the Tower and the West Wing of Royal Victoria College form part of the university's residence system. In 1900, the university established the MacLennan Travelling Library. <i>McGill University waltz</i> composed by Frances C. Robinson, was published in Montr&eacute;al by W.H. Scroggie, c 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal,_Montreal_(HS85-10-17321).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/300px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg" width="300" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/450px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/600px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal,_Montreal_(HS85-10-17321).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> McGill University and Mount Royal, 1906, Panoramic Photo Company
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1905, the university acquired a second campus when <a href="/wiki/William_Christopher_Macdonald" title="William Christopher Macdonald">Sir William C. Macdonald</a>, one of the university's major benefactors, endowed a college in Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, 32 kilometres west of Montreal. Macdonald College, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a>, opened to students in 1907, originally offering programs in agriculture, household science, and teaching.</p> 
     <p>McGill was instrumental in founding several universities. It established the first post-secondary institutions in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> to provide degree programs to the growing cities of <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria</a>. It chartered <a href="/wiki/Victoria_College,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria College, British Columbia">Victoria College</a> in 1903, a two-year college offering first and second-year McGill courses in arts and science, which was the predecessor institution to the modern <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">University of Victoria</a>. The province's first university was incorporated in Vancouver in 1908 as the McGill University College of British Columbia. The private institution granted McGill degrees until it became the independent <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">University of British Columbia</a> in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dawson_College" title="Dawson College">Dawson College</a> was set up by McGill as a satellite campus in 1945 to handle the overflow registration of students after the Second World War and the returning veterans. Many students in their first 3 years in the Faculty of Engineering took courses at Dawson College to relieve the McGill campus for the later 2 years for their degree course. Dawson eventually became independent of McGill and evolved into the first English <a href="/wiki/CEGEP" title="CEGEP">CEGEP</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>. In addition, McGill alumnus and professor, Dr. <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, and Dr. <a href="/wiki/Howard_Atwood_Kelly" title="Howard Atwood Kelly">Howard Atwood Kelly</a>, also a former professor of medicine at McGill, were very much involved in the creation of the medical school of <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins University</a>. Osler became the first Physician-in-Chief of the new <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, Maryland, USA in 1889, and was instrumental in the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine" class="mw-redirect">Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine</a> in 1893. He and Kelly were also among the Johns Hopkins' earliest professors of medicine.</p> 
     <p>George Allan Ross (architect) designed the Pathology Building, 1922–23; the Neurological Institute, 1933; Neurological Institute addition 1938 at McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Jean Julien Perrault (architect) designed the <a href="/wiki/McTavish_Street" title="McTavish Street">McTavish Street</a> residence for Charles E. Gravel, which is now called David Thompson House (1934).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University,_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg/220px-McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" width="220" height="345" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg/330px-McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg/440px-McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University,_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> McGill University, Stained Glass Great War Memorial (Delta Upsilon) entrance to the Blackader-Lauterman Library of Architecture and Art
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The War Memorial Hall (more generally known as Memorial Hall) is a landmark building on the campus of McGill University. At the dedication ceremony the Governor General of Canada (<a href="/wiki/Harold_Alexander,_1st_Earl_Alexander_of_Tunis" title="Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis">Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis</a>) laid the cornerstone. Dedicated on October 6, 1946, the Memorial Hall and adjoining Memorial Pool honour students who had enlisted and died in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War" class="mw-redirect">First World War</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War" class="mw-redirect">Second World War</a>. In Memorial Hall, there are two Stained Glass Regimental badge World War I and World War II Memorial Windows by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> c. 1950/1.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> A war memorial window (1950) by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> in the McGill War Memorial Hall depicts the figure of St. Michael and the badges of the Navy, Army and the Air Force. 23 members of the McGill Chapter of Delta Upsilon who gave their lives in the Great War. A Great War memorial window featuring Saint George and a slain dragon at the entrance to the Blackader-Lauterman Library of Architecture and Art is dedicated to the memory of 23 members of the McGill Chapter of Delta Upsilon who gave their lives in the Great War.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Six other windows (1951) by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> on the west wall of the memorial hall depict the coats of arms of the regiments in which the McGill alumni were members. There is a memorial archway at <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_College" title="Macdonald College" class="mw-redirect">Macdonald College</a>, two additional floors added to the existing Sir <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Currie" title="Arthur Currie">Arthur Currie</a> gymnasium, a hockey rink and funding for an annual Memorial Assembly. A Book of Remembrance on a marble table contains the names of those lost in both World Wars. On 11 November 2012 the McGill Remembers web site launched; the University War Records Office collected documents between 1940-1946 related to McGill students, staff and faculty in the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Board_of_Canada" title="National Film Board of Canada">National Film Board of Canada</a> documentary `Occupation` (1970), directed by Bill Reid, documents the occupation of the offices of the Political Science Department at McGill University in 1970 by striking political science students.`<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_University_Companies_-_McGill_in_the_Great_War_1914-1918">The University Companies - McGill in the Great War 1914-1918</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The University Companies - McGill in the Great War 1914-1918">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/220px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/330px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/440px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> This photo was taken at McGill University in Montreal in 1915 before the departure of the 2nd University Company for France. The Company reinforced Princess Patricia's Canadian Light Infantry on the Somme in October 1915
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>McGill University played a unique role in the Great War. Many students and alumni of course enlisted in the first wave of patriotic fervor that swept the nation in 1914. McGill’s unique role emerged in the spring of 1915 after the first wave of heavy Canadian casualties at Ypres. The Canadian Divisions had been badly mauled and six thousand reinforcements were needed every three months. But Princess Patricia’s Canadian Light Infantry were not part of that reinforcement scheme. As the first Canadian regiment in action, the Patricia’s had been serving as part of a British Brigade. Although reinforcements trickled into the Patricia’s, the priority for Canada was keeping the First Division up to strength and getting a Third Division ready for deployment. For the completer story of the Regiment in the Great War.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Faced with a desperate shortage of troops, Hamilton Gault, the founder of the regiment and a wealthy Montreal businessman reached out to his friends at home for support. In early 1915, the government had authorized the formation of a company at McGill University for the 38th Battalion being formed in Ottawa. With news of the devastating losses to the Patricia’s at Frezenberg, three prominent McGill graduates, George MacDonald, George Currie and Percival Molson, suggested that the University companies be used to reinforce the Patricia’s. All were prominent and wealthy Montreal businessmen. Molson was also well known as an athlete having completed in hockey, football and track and field. The first two companies had joined the new Canadian Officers Training Corps concentrating at Niagara-on-the-Lake for training. In short order, they were on their way to France. The First Company joined the Regiment at Armentieres in late July and the second arrived little more than a month later. Fortunately, the summer of 1915 was relatively quiet. As those recovering from injury returned and the new arrivals were absorbed, a very different regiment emerged. In total 1300 men from five University Companies joined the Regiment between July 1915 and June 1916. The program initiated at McGill reached out to other Canadian Universities and affiliated colleges across the country to attract recruits. As a group, they were younger, better educated and more likely to be Canadian born than the originals. A full eighteen percent would ultimately become officers with most of those being commissioned from the ranks. Although over two hundred were commissioned from the ranks many more would serve as soldiers in the ranks throughout the war. Those historians who suggest that such reinforcement was a waste of talent show a profound lack of understanding about what is required for leadership in combat. In an era, when only 15% of males between 15 and 20 were in school, attendance at university had more to do with family position than innate talent. The training provided to those who were commissioned before joining their regiments was often sadly lacking. Most learned the essentials of leadership after they had joined their regiment in the field, learning from those more experienced in how to survive trench warfare. Writing to his wife in September 1915, Agar Adamson described the new arrivals: “I find a great change in the Regiment and the new N.C.O.s of the two McGill Companies are sadly wanting in experience and in some cases may be a positive danger.&quot; <sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> By January 1916, after some time in the trenches given the regiment an opportunity to assess the leadership merits of the new arrivals, the Regiment was being asked to find a hundred NCOs who might be commissioned to fill the needs of other regiments. At Vimy and Passchendaele in 1917, men from the university companies were leading the attacking companies and McDonald, Currie and Molson had all been awarded the Military Cross for bravery in action. On their return to Canada after the war, Major George McDonald and Major George Currie went on to for the accounting firm McDonald Currie that later became one of the founding groups on Price Waterhouse Coopers.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Captain <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson" title="Percival Molson">Percival Molson</a> was killed in action in July 1917. <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Percival Molson Memorial Stadium</a> at McGill is named in his honour.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Students">Students</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Students">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Proud_graduates.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/220px-Proud_graduates.jpg" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/330px-Proud_graduates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/440px-Proud_graduates.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Proud_graduates.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Ph.D. candidates march at Commencement in McGill's 
        <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_(color)" title="Scarlet (color)">scarlet</a> regalia.
        <sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>McGill's student population includes 25,938 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate" title="Undergraduate" class="mw-redirect">undergraduate</a> and 8,881 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student" class="mw-redirect">graduate students</a> representing diverse geographic and linguistic backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Of the entire student population, 54.7% are from Quebec and 25.4% are from the rest of Canada, while 20.0% are from outside of Canada (including the United States). International students hail from about 150 different countries,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> with Americans comprising about half of all international undergraduates and a third of all international postgraduates in the entering class of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Almost half of McGill students claim a first language other than English. While the university is located in a Francophone province, only 17.8% of the students claim French as their mother tongue, compared to 51.8% who claim English and 30.5% who claim some other language.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_schools">Faculties and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Faculties and schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In the 2007–2008 school year, McGill offered over 340 academic programs in eleven faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-students_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-students-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also offers over 250 doctoral and master's graduate degree programs. Despite strong increases in university enrollment across North America,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill has upheld a relatively low<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> and appealing student-faculty ratio of 16:1.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> There are nearly 1,600 <a href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure" class="mw-redirect">tenured</a> or tenure-track professors and 4,300 adjunct and visiting professors teaching at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-facultystaff_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facultystaff-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>22% of all students are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Arts" title="McGill University Faculty of Arts">Faculty of Arts</a>, McGill's largest academic unit. Of the other larger faculties, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Science" title="McGill University Faculty of Science">Faculty of Science</a> enrolls 15%, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Medicine" title="McGill University Faculty of Medicine">Faculty of Medicine</a> enrolls 13%, the Centre for Continuing Education enrolls 12%, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="McGill University Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a> enrol about 10% each.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The remainder of all students are enrolled in McGill's smaller schools, including the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Agricultural_and_Environmental_Sciences" title="McGill University Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Dentistry" title="McGill University Faculty of Dentistry">Faculty of Dentistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Education" title="McGill University Faculty of Education">Faculty of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Law" title="McGill University Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Music" title="Schulich School of Music">Schulich School of Music</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Religious_Studies" title="McGill University Faculty of Religious Studies">Faculty of Religious Studies</a>. Since the 1880s,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill has been affiliated with three <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">Theological Colleges</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Montreal" title="Anglican Diocese of Montreal">Montreal Diocesan</a> Theological College (<a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican Church of Canada</a>), <a href="/wiki/The_Presbyterian_College,_Montreal" title="The Presbyterian College, Montreal">The Presbyterian College, Montreal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Canada" title="Presbyterian Church in Canada">Presbyterian Church in Canada</a>), and United Theological College (<a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's Faculty of Religious Studies maintains additional affiliations with other theological institutions and organizations, such as the Montreal School of Theology.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Schools at the university include the School of Architecture, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_School_of_Computer_Science" title="McGill University School of Computer Science">School of Computer Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_School_of_Information_Studies" title="McGill University School of Information Studies">School of Information Studies</a>, the School of Dietetics and Human Nutrition, the School of Physical &amp; Occupational Therapy, the Ingram School of Nursing, the School of Social Work, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_%E2%80%93_School_of_Urban_Planning" title="McGill University – School of Urban Planning" class="mw-redirect">School of Urban Planning</a>, and the McGill School of Environment. They also include the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Institute_of_Islamic_Studies" title="McGill University Institute of Islamic Studies">Institute of Islamic Studies</a> (established in 1952) which offers graduate courses leading to the M.A. and Ph.D. degrees, and covering the history, culture, and civilization of Islam since its inception and up to modern times; the Institute is also served by one of the richest libraries in North America on Islamic studies with sources in many languages. The Graduate and Postdoctoral Studies<sup id="cite_ref-gps_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gps-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> (GPS) oversees the admission and registration of graduate students (both master's and Ph.D.). The GPS administers graduate fellowships, postdoctoral affairs, and the graduation process, including the examination of theses. In conjunction with other units, it conducts regular program reviews in all study disciplines.</p> 
     <p>Founded in 1956, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Executive_Institute" title="McGill Executive Institute">McGill Executive Institute</a> provides business seminars and custom executive education to companies, government services and non-profit organizations. Led primarily by McGill faculty, the executive courses and management training programs are designed for all managerial levels, from board members to senior-level executives to junior managers.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centres_and_institutes">Research centres and institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Research centres and institutes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Research plays a critical role at McGill. According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>, &quot;Researchers at McGill are affiliated with about 75 major research centres and networks, and are engaged in an extensive array of research partnerships with other universities, government and industry in Quebec and Canada, throughout North America and in dozens of other countries.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Annually, around 100 inventions take place at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-research07-08_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-research07-08-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In recognition of its research quality, McGill is affiliated with 12 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureate" title="Nobel Laureate" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Laureates</a> and professors have won major teaching prizes. McGill's researchers are supported by the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Library" title="McGill University Library">McGill University Library</a>, which comprises 13 branch libraries and holds over six million items.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 1926, McGill has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU), an organization of leading research universities in North America. McGill is also a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international network of leading research-intensive universities that work together to expand their global reach and advance their plans for internationalization.</p> 
     <p>McGill is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group of prominent research universities within Canada. <a href="/wiki/McGill-Queen%27s_University_Press" title="McGill-Queen's University Press">McGill-Queen's University Press</a> began as McGill in 1963 and amalgamated with Queen's in 1969. McGill-Queen's University Press focuses on Canadian studies and publishes the Canadian Public Administration Series.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/220px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/330px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/440px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Radon, discovered at McGill by physicist Ernest Rutherford
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>McGill is perhaps best recognized for its research and discoveries in the health sciences. <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilder_Penfield" title="Wilder Penfield">Wilder Penfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Olding_Hebb" title="Donald Olding Hebb" class="mw-redirect">Donald Hebb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Milner" title="Brenda Milner">Brenda Milner</a>, and others made significant discoveries in <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> while working at McGill. The <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Institute" title="Montreal Neurological Institute" class="mw-redirect">Montreal Neurological Institute</a> is also located in McGill university, where many of these individuals worked. The first hormone governing the Immune System (later christened the Cytokine 'Interleukin-2') was discovered at McGill in 1965 by Gordon &amp; McLean.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The invention of the world's first artificial cell was made by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chang" title="Thomas Chang">Thomas Chang</a>, an undergraduate student at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> While chair of physics at McGill, nuclear physicist <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> performed the experiment that led to the discovery of the alpha particle and its function in radioactive decay, which won him the Nobel Prize in Chemistry in 1908. Alumnus Jack Szostak, now a professor of genetics at Massachusetts General Hospital in Boston, was awarded the 2009 Nobel Prize in medicine for discovering a key mechanism in the genetic operations of cells, an insight that has inspired new lines of research into cancer.</p> 
     <p>William Chalmers invented <a href="/wiki/Plexiglas" title="Plexiglas" class="mw-redirect">Plexiglas</a> while a graduate student at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In computing, <a href="/wiki/MUSIC/SP" title="MUSIC/SP">MUSIC/SP</a>, software for mainframes once popular among universities and colleges around the world, was developed at McGill. A team also contributed to the development of <a href="/wiki/Archie_search_engine" title="Archie search engine">Archie</a>, a pre-<a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">WWW</a> search engine. A 3270 terminal emulator developed at McGill was commercialized and later sold to Hummingbird Software.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries.2C_Archives_and_Museums">Libraries, Archives and Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Libraries, Archives and Museums">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The McGill University Libraries, Department of Rare Books &amp; Special Collections consist of 350,000 items, mainly books, manuscripts, maps, prints, and a general rare book collection. In the Main Hall of the Library, exhibitions publicize the 50 special collections.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The McGill University Archives house official records of, or relating to, or people/activities connected with McGill University. The collection consists of manuscripts, texts, photographs, audio-visual material, architectural records, cartographic materials, prints and drawings, microforms and artifacts.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>]</p> 
     <p>The McGill Medical Museum catalogues, preserves, conserves and displays collections that documents the study and practice of medicine at McGill University and its associated teaching hospitals. The Medical museum features collections, individual specimens, artifacts, equipment log books/autopsy journals/paper materials and medical instruments and apparati, 25 wax models, 200 mostly skeletal dry specimens; and 400 lantern slides of anatomic specimens. There is a special emphasis on pathology; there are 2000 fluid filled-preserved anatomical and pathological specimens. The Osler collection, for example consists of 60 wet specimens while The Abbott collection consists of 80 wet specimens, mostly examples of congenital cardiac disease.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> ranked McGill first in the category of Canadian medical-doctoral universities for the eighth consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada#Higher_Education_Strategy_Associates.27_rankings" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">Higher Education Strategy Associates</a> ranked McGill sixth nationally in Science and Engineering and second nationally in Social Sciences and Humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Gourman_Ranking_of_Canadian_Universities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Gourman Ranking of Canadian Universities (page does not exist)">The Gourman Ranking of Canadian Universities</a> also ranked McGill first in Canada in its 1998 report on undergraduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill was ranked the best university in Canada, and 17th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-theqs2009_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theqs2009-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill was also ranked 15th in the world for Employer Reputation by Q.S.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Within specific fields, in 2009 McGill ranked 10th in the <a href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">life sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biomedicine" title="Biomedicine">biomedicine</a>, 14th in the <a href="/wiki/Arts" title="Arts" class="mw-redirect">arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>, 17th in the <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences" class="mw-redirect">social sciences</a>, 26th in the <a href="/wiki/Natural_sciences" title="Natural sciences" class="mw-redirect">natural sciences</a>, and 20th in <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-theqs2008_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theqs2008-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> When McGill placed 12th overall in the 2007 ranking, the achievement was regarded as the &quot;highest rank to be reached by a Canadian institution.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill ranked 34th in the world and third in Canada according to the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> published in 2012, McGill ranked third in Canada and 63th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the most recent ranking of world universities by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>, McGill university is ranked 17th.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the Trendence/Emerging Global Employability Ranking, based on a survey of hundreds of major employers in 10 different countries, ranked schools according to their perceived popularity among major job recruiters. McGill placed 19th in the world for employability in this ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-NYtimes_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYtimes-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2008 <a href="/wiki/College_Prowler" title="College Prowler">College Prowler Online</a> rankings for Academics at North American universities, McGill earned an A- for Academics; making it the only Canadian school to achieve a <a href="/wiki/Grade_(education)#United_States" title="Grade (education)" class="mw-redirect">grade</a> above a B-.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2009, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> ranked McGill's business school, the <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a>, 11th in the world among non-U.S. universities for its two-year MBA program.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a></i> Ranking placed the Desautels Faculty of Management of McGill University first in Canada and 8th in the world among business schools.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Financial_Times" title="The Financial Times" class="mw-redirect">The Financial Times</a></i>, in its global MBA ranking, placed Desautels 44th in the world in 2006 and 57th in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The ranking placed it 33rd and 31st worldwide in the value for money and alumni recommended categories respectively. In <a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect">BusinessWeek</a>'s Best International B-Schools Of 2008, Desautels was ranked among the top 16 international business schools, ranking fourth in intellectual capital with a selectivity of 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since <i>Maclean's</i> began ranking Canadian law schools in 2007, it has placed McGill's law school second overall for the second year in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-toplawschools_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toplawschools-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lawranking_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lawranking-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, McGill's law school, which requires reading knowledge of French and offers the joint <a href="/wiki/B.C.L." title="B.C.L." class="mw-redirect">B.C.L.</a>/<a href="/wiki/LL.B." title="LL.B." class="mw-redirect">LL.B.</a> degree in both civil law and common law, ranked first by supreme court clerkships, second by elite firm hiring, third by faculty hiring, fourth by faculty <a href="/wiki/Journal_Citation_Reports" title="Journal Citation Reports">journal citations</a>, and eighth by national reach.<sup id="cite_ref-lawranking2_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lawranking2-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></i>s Canadian University Report awarded McGill top marks in its 2008 annual university survey. McGill received an A+ for Academic Reputation, the highest score of any large, medium, or small sized University. Additionally the school received an A- for: most satisfied students, quality of education, extracurricular activities, recreation and athletics, and campus atmosphere; as well as A's in both library services and campus technology. The Canadian University Report awarded McGill's downtown campus a D for its 'on-campus' food services and a C for its on-campus pub Gerts.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_2">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Research Infosource named McGill &quot;Research University of the Year&quot; in its 2003 and 2005 rankings of Canada's Top 50 Research Universities.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rstop50rutyl_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rstop50rutyl-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Research Infosource ranked McGill the second-best research university in the country, after the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rstop50rutyl_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rstop50rutyl-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> They also ranked McGill University third in Canada in research-intensity and fourth in total-research funding,<sup id="cite_ref-rstop50rul_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rstop50rul-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> finding that McGill ranks in the top five universities in terms of research dollars per full-time faculty member and number of refereed publications per full-time faculty member. The study showed that research funding represents approximately $259,100 per faculty member, the fourth highest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-rstop50rul_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rstop50rul-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>McGill was named one of &quot;<a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Top_100_Employers" title="Canada's Top 100 Employers">Canada's Top 100 Employers</a>&quot; in October 2008 and October 2009 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mediacorp_Canada_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mediacorp Canada Inc. (page does not exist)">Mediacorp Canada Inc.</a>, and was featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> newsmagazine.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Endowments_Institute" title="Sustainable Endowments Institute" class="mw-redirect">Sustainable Endowments Institute</a> gave McGill a grade of &quot;B&quot; on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2009_College_Sustainability_Report_Card&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2009 College Sustainability Report Card (page does not exist)">2009 College Sustainability Report Card</a> for its improvements in on-campus environmental sustainability,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> with only 34 schools earning higher grade.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> magazine, in its May 2006 issue, ranked McGill as the tenth best <a href="/wiki/Party_school" title="Party school">party school</a> in North America. McGill was the only Canadian university in the list.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>For Fall 2012, McGill accepted 14,220 (45.8%) of 31,049 undergraduate applicants, and 3,618 (32.1%) of 11,266 graduate applicants; about 6,000 undergraduates and 2,000 graduates matriculate each year.<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Among admitted students, the median Quebec <a href="/wiki/CEGEP" title="CEGEP">CEGEP</a> <a href="/wiki/R-score" title="R-score" class="mw-redirect">r-score</a> was 30.1, while the median grade 12 averages for students entering McGill from outside of Quebec ranged between 92% and 93% (A).<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> For American students, the median <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores in the verbal, math, and writing sections were 690, 700, and 690 respectively, for a combined SAT score of around 2080; the median <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> score was 31.</p> 
     <p>For law students, the median undergraduate GPA was 85% (or 3.7 on a 4.0 scale) and the median LSAT score was 163 (88.1th percentile) out of a possible 180 points.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> For medical students, the median undergraduate GPA was 3.8 out of 4.0 and the median MCAT score was 32.1.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the 30% of applicants admitted to the Desautels Faculty of Management's MBA program, applicants had, on average, a <a href="/wiki/GMAT" title="GMAT" class="mw-redirect">GMAT</a> score of 665, an age of 27, and 49 months of work experience.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_campus">Downtown campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Downtown campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/220px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/330px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/440px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg 2x" /></a>

     </div>

       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> McGill's downtown campus at night viewed from 
        <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a>. The circular building in the foreground is the McIntyre Medical Sciences Building.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>McGill's main campus is situated in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Montreal" title="Downtown Montreal">downtown Montreal</a> at the foot of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of its buildings are situated in a park-like campus located north of <a href="/wiki/Sherbrooke_Street" title="Sherbrooke Street">Sherbrooke Street</a> and south of Pine Ave between <a href="/wiki/Peel_Street,_Montreal" title="Peel Street, Montreal">Peel</a> and Aylmer streets. The campus also extends west of Peel for several blocks, starting north of Docteur-Penfield. The campus is near the <a href="/wiki/Peel_(Montreal_Metro)" title="Peel (Montreal Metro)">Peel</a> and <a href="/wiki/McGill_(Montreal_Metro)" title="McGill (Montreal Metro)">McGill</a> <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">metro</a> stations. All of the major university buildings were constructed using local grey limestone, which serves as a unifying element.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's first classes were held in at Burnside Place, James McGill's country home.<sup id="cite_ref-Kip_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kip-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Burnside Place remained the sole educational facility until the 1840s, when the school began construction on its first buildings: the central and east wings of the Arts Building.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The rest of the campus was essentially a cow <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a>, a situation similar to the few other Canadian universities and early American colleges of the age.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's athletic facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Molson_Stadium" title="Molson Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Molson Stadium</a>, are located on Mount Royal, near the residence halls and the Montreal Neurological Institute. The Gymnasium is named in honour of General <a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_William_Currie" title="Sir Arthur William Currie" class="mw-redirect">Sir Arthur William Currie</a>.</p>
