     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Residence">Residence</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Residence">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>McGill's residence system is relatively small for a school of its size, housing approximately 2,700 undergraduate students and a handful of graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Most McGill students do not live in <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">residence</a> (known <a href="/wiki/Colloquialism" title="Colloquialism">colloquially</a> as &quot;rez&quot;) after their first year of study, even if they are not from the Montreal area. With the exception of students returning as &quot;floor fellows&quot; or &quot;dons&quot;, the majority of McGill residences are for first-year undergraduate students only. Senior students are expected to find off-campus housing.</p> 
     <p>Many first-year students live in the Bishop Mountain Residences (&quot;Upper Rez&quot;),<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> a series of concrete dormitories on the slope of Mount Royal, consisting of <a href="/wiki/John_Wilson_McConnell" title="John Wilson McConnell">McConnell Hall</a>, Molson Hall, Gardner Hall, and Douglas Hall. Douglas Hall, which opened in 1937, is distinguished by its impressive stone facade and wood interiors. McConnell, Molson, and Gardner Halls, all built in the 1960s, share a <a href="/wiki/Cafeteria" title="Cafeteria">cafeteria</a>, located at the centre of the three dormitories, known as Bishop Mountain Hall.</p> 
     <p><i>Royal Victoria College</i>, the second-largest residence at McGill, was a women's only dormitory; however in September 2010 the dormitory became co-ed. One of <a href="/wiki/Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll" title="Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll">Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll</a>`s works as a sculptor is the statue of her Royal mother <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> erected in front of the Royal Victoria College, Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Other old residences located just north of <i>RVC</i> are: &quot;Pres Hall&quot; and &quot;Uni Hall&quot; (short for University and also known as Dio). Both residences are small and adjacent to churches, Pres Hall being adjacent to the Presbyterian Church and Uni Hall adjacent to the Diocesan Theological College.</p> 
     <p>McGill's second newest residence, aptly named <i>New Residence Hall</i> (&quot;New Rez&quot;) is a converted four-star hotel located a few blocks east of campus. New Rez is the largest of the university's dormitories.</p> 
     <p>'McGill also offers more independent living style residences, this includes 'Solin Hall<i>, an apartment-style residence four <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">metro</a> stops from campus. The McGill Off-Campus Residence Experience (MORE) residences consist of a series of converted apartment buildings and houses, the largest of which is The Greenbriar, an apartment-style residence located across from the Milton Gates.</i></p> 
     <p>In autumn 2008, due to increased demand for first-year housing, the University chose to lease four floors of a privately owned apartment building for use as a university residence. The building, called &quot;515 Ste. Catherine&quot;, is on the corner of Rue Ste. Catherine and Rue City Councillors, close to campus yet in the heart of downtown Montreal. It was completely renovated and featured a gym, movie theater, and fully furnished apartments. However, the McGill Residence Office decided to forgo use of the building after summer 2009. In April 2009, McGill acquired the Four Points Sheraton Hotel at 475 Sherbrooke Street West. The hotel was converted into a new student residence, which opened in fall 2009. Although it is the newest residence, students either call it Carrefour, or, informally, &quot;C4.&quot; Officially, however, the building has been named Carrefour Sherbrooke Residence Hall.</p> 
     <p>Most second-year students transition to off-campus apartment housing, and apartment hunting is sometimes seen as a rite of passage for McGill students. Many students end up living in the &quot;<a href="/wiki/McGill_Ghetto" title="McGill Ghetto">McGill Ghetto</a>&quot;, the neighbourhood directly to the east of the downtown campus. In recent years, finding affordable housing has been challenging because of the city's tight housing market, particularly in neighbourhoods close to the McGill campus.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Students have begun moving out to other areas because of rising rent prices.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Master_plan">Master plan</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Master plan">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>McGill has begun an ambitious process to lay the groundwork for future development. A Task Force on Campus Planning has been created to study the issue. It has begun to consult widely within the McGill and greater community on a broad range of issues including community life, physical development plans, and other issues. Its recommendations include how McGill can develop in a way that supports the University’s mission and goals, and continues to benefit and bring value to the surrounding areas and the greater Montreal community. Among the guiding principles of the Task Force’s work are commitment to community, responsible stewardship, maintenance of green space and the integrity of the mountain, and the preservation of heritage architectural assets.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>One recent initiative turned McGill into a car-free campus.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Redevelopment_plan.2C_McGill_University_Health_Centre">Redevelopment plan, McGill University Health Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Redevelopment plan, McGill University Health Centre">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In 2006, the Quebec government initiated a $1.6 billion <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> redevelopment project for the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Health_Centre" title="McGill University Health Centre">McGill University Health Centre</a> (MUHC). The project will expand facilities to two separate campuses<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> and consolidate the various hospitals of the MUHC on the site of an old <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">CP</a> <a href="/wiki/Rail_yard" title="Rail yard">rail yard</a> adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Vend%C3%B4me_(Montreal_Metro)" title="Vend&ocirc;me (Montreal Metro)">Vend&ocirc;me</a> <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">metro</a> station. This site, known as Glen Yards, comprises 170,000 square metres (1,800,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) and spans portions of Montreal's <a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame-de-Gr%C3%A2ce" title="Notre-Dame-de-Gr&acirc;ce">Notre-Dame-de-Gr&acirc;ce</a> neighbourhood and the city of <a href="/wiki/Westmount,_Quebec" title="Westmount, Quebec">Westmount</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The Glen Yards project has been controversial due to local opposition to the project, environmental issues, and the cost of the project itself.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The project, which has received approval from the provincial government, was, in 2003, expected to be complete by 2010. The new 'campus' is now expected to open in 2014 or 2015.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macdonald_campus">Macdonald campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Macdonald campus">edit</a>]</span></h3>

      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A second campus, the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue,_Quebec" title="Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, Quebec">Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue</a> houses the Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Science, the School of Dietetics and Human Nutrition, the Institute of Parasitology, and the McGill School of Environment. The <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Arboretum" title="Morgan Arboretum">Morgan Arboretum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/J._S._Marshall_Radar_Observatory" title="J. S. Marshall Radar Observatory">J. S. Marshall Radar Observatory</a> are nearby.</p> 
     <p>The Morgan <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">Arboretum</a> was created in 1945. It is a 2.5-square-kilometre (0.965&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) forested reserve with the aim of 'teaching, research, and public education'. Its mandated research goals are to continue research related to maintaining the health of the Arboretum <a href="/wiki/Plantations" title="Plantations" class="mw-redirect">plantations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woodlands</a>, to develop new programs related to selecting <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">adapted</a> to developing environmental conditions and to develop silvicultural practices that preserve and enhance <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a> in both natural stands and plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2007, McGill premiered its Office of Sustainability and added a second full-time position in this area, the Director of Sustainability in addition to the Sustainability Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainability_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainability-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Recent efforts in implementing its sustainable development plan include the new Life Sciences Center which was built with LEED-Silver certification and a green roof, as well as an increase in parking rates in January 2008 to fund other sustainability projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainability_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainability-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Other student projects include The Flat: Bike Collective, which promotes alternative transportation, and the Farmer's Market, which occurs during the fall harvest.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Sustainability:_Campus_Committees_and_Groups_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Sustainability:_Campus_Committees_and_Groups-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> The Farmer's Market and many other initiatives came out of student collaboration during the Rethink Conference 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Sustainability:_Rethink_Forms_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Sustainability:_Rethink_Forms-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>McGill's <a href="/wiki/Bellairs_Research_Institute" title="Bellairs Research Institute">Bellairs Research Institute</a>, located in St. James, Barbados <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McGill_University&amp;params=13_10_N_59_35_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">13&deg;10′N</span> <span class="longitude">59&deg;35′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">13.167&deg;N 59.583&deg;W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">13.167; -59.583</span></span></span></a></span>, is Canada's only teaching and research facility in the tropics.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> The institute has been in use for over 50 years. Its facilities are regularly utilized by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">Canadian Space Agency</a> for research.</p> 
     <p>The laboratories of the <a href="/wiki/Huntsman_Marine_Science_Centre" title="Huntsman Marine Science Centre">Huntsman Marine Science Centre</a> are located in <a href="/wiki/St._Andrews,_New_Brunswick" title="St. Andrews, New Brunswick">St. Andrews, N.B.</a>, on 300,000 square metres (3,200,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) of land at the <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> of the <a href="/wiki/St._Croix_River_(Maine-New_Brunswick)" title="St. Croix River (Maine-New Brunswick)" class="mw-redirect">St. Croix River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> It hosts the Atlantic Reference Centre, which is known throughout the <a href="/wiki/Maritimes" title="Maritimes" class="mw-redirect">Maritimes</a> for its extensive marine biology collections.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The HMS is a research facility &quot;committed to the advancement of the marine sciences through basic and applied research&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> and acts as a field facility for research and teaching by McGill and other member universities.</p> 
     <p>McGill's Gault <a href="/wiki/Nature_Reserve" title="Nature Reserve" class="mw-redirect">Nature Reserve</a> <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McGill_University&amp;params=45_32_N_73_10_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">45&deg;32′N</span> <span class="longitude">73&deg;10′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">45.533&deg;N 73.167&deg;W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">45.533; -73.167</span></span></span></a></span> spans over 10 square kilometres (3.9&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of forest land, the largest remaining remnant of the <a href="/wiki/Old_growth_forest" title="Old growth forest" class="mw-redirect">primeval forests</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> The first scientific studies at the site occurred in 1859. The site has been the site of extensive research activities: &quot;Today there are over 400 scientific articles, 100 graduate theses, more than 50 government reports and about 30 book chapters that are based on research at <a href="/wiki/Mont-Saint-Hilaire,_Quebec" title="Mont-Saint-Hilaire, Quebec">Mont St. Hilaire</a>.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition to the McGill University Health Centre, McGill has been directly partnered with many <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospitals</a> for decades, and also has a history of collaborating with many hospitals in Montreal. These cooperations allow the university to graduate over 1,000 students in <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> each year.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill's contract-affiliated teaching hospitals include: <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Montreal Children's Hospital">Montreal Children's Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_General_Hospital" title="Montreal General Hospital">Montreal General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Hospital" title="Montreal Neurological Hospital" class="mw-redirect">Montreal Neurological Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Chest_Institute" title="Montreal Chest Institute">Montreal Chest Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Hospital,_Montreal" title="Royal Victoria Hospital, Montreal">Royal Victoria Hospital</a> which are all now part of the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Health_Centre" title="McGill University Health Centre">McGill University Health Centre</a>. Other hospitals that health care students may use include: <a href="/wiki/Sir_Mortimer_B._Davis_Jewish_General_Hospital" title="Sir Mortimer B. Davis Jewish General Hospital" class="mw-redirect">Sir Mortimer B. Davis – Jewish General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Hospital" title="Douglas Hospital" class="mw-redirect">Douglas Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Hospital_(Montreal)" title="St. Mary's Hospital (Montreal)">St. Mary's Hospital Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Until the late 19th century, McGill had also owned parkland atop the <a href="/wiki/Westmount_Summit" title="Westmount Summit">Westmount Summit</a>, which was used as a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>. In the early twentieth century, McGill donated the land to the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westmount" title="City of Westmount" class="mw-redirect">City of Westmount</a> on the condition that it become a <a href="/wiki/Bird_sanctuary" title="Bird sanctuary" class="mw-redirect">bird sanctuary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Les_amis_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Les_amis-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="University_identity_and_culture">University identity and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: University identity and culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mcgill_CoA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Mcgill_CoA.jpg/170px-Mcgill_CoA.jpg" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Mcgill_CoA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Mcgill_CoA.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mcgill_CoA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> McGill’s coat of arms
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The McGill <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> is derived from an armorial device assumed during his lifetime by the founder of the University, James McGill. The University's patent of arms was granted by England's Garter-King-at-Arms in 1922 and registered in 1956 with Lord Lyon King of Arms in Edinburgh and in 1992 with the Public Register of Arms, Flags and Badges of Canada. In heraldic terms, the coat of arms is described as follows: &quot;Argent three Martlets Gules, on a chief dancette of the second, an open book proper garnished or bearing the legend <i>In Domino Confido</i> in letters Sable between two crowns of the first. Motto: <i>Grandescunt Aucta Labore</i>.&quot; The coat of arms consists of two parts, the shield and the scroll. The University publishes a guide to the use of the University's arms and motto.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's symbol is the <a href="/wiki/Martlet" title="Martlet">martlet</a>, stemming from the presence of the mythical bird on the official <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">arms</a> of the university. The school's official colours are red and white. McGill's motto is <i>Grandescunt Aucta Labore</i>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language" class="mw-redirect">Latin</a> for &quot;By work, all things increase and grow&quot; (literally, &quot;Things grown great increase by work,&quot; that is, things that grow to be great do so by means of work).</p> 
     <p>The official <a href="/wiki/School_song" title="School song">school song</a> is entitled &quot;Hail, <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater" title="Alma Mater" class="mw-redirect">Alma Mater</a>.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's color is scarlet, which figures prominently in the <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress_of_McGill_University" title="Academic dress of McGill University">academic dress of McGill University</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_policy">Language policy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Language policy">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Though McGill allowed students to write graduation theses in French as early as 1835, McGill never became a Francophone or officially <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" title="Bilingual" class="mw-redirect">bilingual</a> university. Today, McGill is one of only three <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English-language</a> universities in Quebec; fluency in French is not a requirement to attend. The Faculty of Law does, however, require all students to be &quot;passively bilingual&quot;, meaning that all students must be able to understand written and spoken French—or English if the student is Francophone—since English or French may be used at any time in a course. Though the University allowed some students to write theses in French from the time the University was founded, since 1964 students in all faculties have been able to write exams and papers in either English or French, provided that the objective of the class is not to learn a particular language.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The 1960s were a period of profound social and political change in Quebec, when English was seen as the privileged language of commerce. McGill, where <a href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">Francophones</a> comprised only three percent of the students, could be seen as the force maintaining economic control by <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_Quebecker" title="English-speaking Quebecker" class="mw-redirect">Anglophones</a> of a predominantly French-speaking province.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i>McGill fran&ccedil;ais</i> movement began in 1969, demanding that McGill become Francophone, pro-nationalist, and pro-worker.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The movement was led by Stanley Gray, a <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a> (and possibly unaware of government plans after the recent (1968) legislation founding the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Universit&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec">Universit&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec</a>). It argued that, since McGill received the lion's share of government funding, paid by a taxpayer base that was largely Francophone, the university should be equally accessible to that segment of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Gray led a demonstration of 10,000 trade unionists, leftist activists, CEGEP students, and even some McGill students, at the university's <a href="/wiki/Roddick_Gates" title="Roddick Gates">Roddick Gates</a> on March 28, 1969. Protesters shouted &quot;McGill fran&ccedil;ais&quot;, &quot;McGill aux Qu&eacute;b&eacute;cois&quot;, and &quot;McGill aux travailleurs&quot; (McGill for workers). However, the majority of students and faculty opposed such a position, and many of the protesters were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> The McGill fran&ccedil;ais protest was, at the time, the second-largest protest in the history of Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Francophone students, whether from Quebec or overseas, now make up approximately 18 percent of the student body, a goal set by the administration partially in the wake of the movement.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> The totally Francophone <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_du_Qu%C3%A9bec_%C3%A0_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Universit&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec &agrave; Montr&eacute;al">Universit&eacute; du Qu&eacute;bec &agrave; Montr&eacute;al</a> had by 2011 an enrollment of 40,000.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The campus has an active <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">students' union</a> represented by the undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Students%27_Society_of_McGill_University" title="Students' Society of McGill University">Students' Society of McGill University</a> (SSMU) and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-Graduate_Students%27_Society_of_McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Post-Graduate Students' Society of McGill University (page does not exist)">Post-Graduate Students' Society of McGill University</a> (PGSS). SSMU was one of the first student societies in Canada to use an <a href="/wiki/Online_voting" title="Online voting" class="mw-redirect">online voting</a> system for campus elections. Due to the large postdoctoral population, the PGSS also contains a semi-autonomous Association of Postdoctoral Fellows (APF). In addition, each faculty has its own student governing body. There are hundreds of clubs and student organizations at the university. Many of them are centred around McGill's student union building, the University Centre. In 1992, students held a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> which called for the University Centre to be named for actor and McGill alumnus <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> The university administration refused to accept the name and did not attend the opening. Traditionally, the administration names buildings in honour of deceased members of the university community or for major <a href="/wiki/Benefactor_(law)" title="Benefactor (law)">benefactors</a>—Shatner is neither.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>McGill has three English-language student-run publications: the <i><a href="/wiki/McGill_Daily" title="McGill Daily" class="mw-redirect">McGill Daily</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/McGill_Tribune" title="McGill Tribune">McGill Tribune</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bull_%26_Bear" title="The Bull &amp; Bear">The Bull &amp; Bear</a></i>. The McGill Daily was first published in 1911. The Daily is currently published twice weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgdaily_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgdaily-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9lit_fran%C3%A7ais" title="D&eacute;lit fran&ccedil;ais" class="mw-redirect">D&eacute;lit fran&ccedil;ais</a></i> is the Daily's French-language counterpart. The combined circulation of both papers is over 28,000.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgdaily_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgdaily-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The McGill Tribune currently publishes once a week, circulating approximately 11,000 copies across campus. The Bull &amp; Bear, operating under the Management Undergraduate Society, publishes 1,000 copies each month<sup id="cite_ref-bullandbear_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullandbear-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> as the only student-run magazine on campus. The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_Foreign_Affairs_Review&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="McGill Foreign Affairs Review (page does not exist)">McGill Foreign Affairs Review</a></i> is a student-run journal about international affairs. Since 1988, <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Red_Herring&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Red Herring (page does not exist)">The Red Herring</a> has been the main satire magazine of McGill University. <a href="/wiki/CKUT" title="CKUT" class="mw-redirect">CKUT</a> (90.3 FM) is the campus radio station. <a href="/wiki/TVMcGill" title="TVMcGill">TVMcGill</a> is the University TV station, broadcasting on closed-circuit television and over the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Law" title="McGill University Faculty of Law">McGill University Faculty of Law</a> is also home to three student-run academic journals, including the world renowned <i><a href="/wiki/McGill_Law_Journal" title="McGill Law Journal">McGill Law Journal</a></i>, founded in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>While <a href="/wiki/Fraternities" title="Fraternities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sororities" title="Sororities" class="mw-redirect">sororities</a> are not a large part of student life at McGill, some, including fraternities <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Upsilon" title="Delta Upsilon">Delta Upsilon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a>, and sororities <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a>, have been established for many years at the university. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Phi_Kappa_Pi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Phi Kappa Pi (page does not exist)">Phi Kappa Pi</a>, Canada's only national fraternity, was founded at McGill and the University of Toronto in 1913 and continues to be active to this day. Events including <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Greece" title="Culture of Greece">Greek</a> week, held annually during the first week of February, have been established to promote Greek life on campus. With just over 2% of the student body population participating, involvement is well below that of most American universities,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> but on par with most Canadian schools.</p> 
     <p>McGill has had a student club supporting <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bisexual" title="Bisexual" class="mw-redirect">bisexual</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">gay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> students since 1972. The group, originally named &quot;Gay McGill&quot;, was renamed &quot;Queer McGill&quot; in 1998 to better identify with the diversity of its members.<sup id="cite_ref-qrep_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrep-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> Queer McGill supports both students and non-student members of the McGill community.<sup id="cite_ref-Queer_McGill_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Queer_McGill-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Membership in 2002 was over 400.<sup id="cite_ref-qrep_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrep-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The three oldest a cappella groups on campus are Tonal Ecstasy, Effusion and Soulstice. These groups perform multiple times during the year at on- and off-campus events.</p> 
     <p>Student organizations at McGill are internationally recognized in a variety of ways. Many larger organizations and <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a> have a local presence on campus. The International Relations Students Association of McGill (IRSAM) currently has consultative status with the UN's <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a> (ECOSOC) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Educational,_Scientific_and_Cultural_Organization" title="United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization" class="mw-redirect">United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization</a> (UNESCO).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1990, IRSAM has hosted an annual <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a>, McMUN, for university students and since 1993 it has hosted an annual <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a>, SSUNS, for high school students.</p> 
     <p>Numerous other humanitarian groups can be found: <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> McGill, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> McGill, <a href="/wiki/End_Poverty_Now" title="End Poverty Now">End Poverty Now</a>, <a href="/wiki/Right_to_Play" title="Right to Play" class="mw-redirect">Right to Play</a> McGill, and <a href="/wiki/Free_the_Children" title="Free the Children">Free the Children</a> are just a few. Numerous student interest groups enhance university life while representing a variety of interests and perspectives.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>McGill is represented in <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a> (CIS) by the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Redmen" title="McGill Redmen">McGill Redmen</a> (men's) and the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Martlets" title="McGill Martlets">McGill Martlets</a> (women's). Following a major restructuring of the varsity programme for the fall semester of 2010, McGill is currently home to 28 varsity teams.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill's unique mascot, Marty the <a href="/wiki/Martlet" title="Martlet">Martlet</a>, was introduced during the 2005 Homecoming game,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The downtown McGill campus sport and exercise facilities include: the McGill Sports Centre (which includes the Tomlinson Fieldhouse and the Windsor Varsity Clinic),<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Molson Stadium</a>, Memorial Pool, Tomlinson Hall, McConnell Arena, Forbes Field, many outdoor <a href="/wiki/Tennis_courts" title="Tennis courts" class="mw-redirect">tennis courts</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Extra-curricular" title="Extra-curricular" class="mw-redirect">extra-curricular</a> <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">arenas</a> and faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> The Macdonald Campus facilities, include an arena, a <a href="/wiki/Gym" title="Gym">gymnasium</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">pool</a>, tennis courts, <a href="/wiki/Fitness_centre" title="Fitness centre" class="mw-redirect">fitness centres</a> and hundreds of acres of green space for regular use.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's largest sporting venue, Molson Stadium, was constructed in 1914. Following an expansion project completed in 2010, it now seats just over 25,000,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> and is the current home field of the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletic_history">Athletic history</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Athletic history">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The inventions of North American <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> are all related to McGill in some way, with <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> rules providing the foundation for the others. Even the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiing</a> has a McGill connection.</p> 
     <p>In 1868, the first recorded game of rugby in North America occurred in Montreal, between British army officers and McGill students,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> giving McGill the oldest university-affiliated rugby club in North America. Other McGill-originated sports evolved out of rugby rules: football, hockey, and basketball. The first game of North American football was played between McGill and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> on May 14, 1874,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> leading to the spread of American football throughout the Ivy League.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> One of the world's first organized hockey clubs, made up of McGill students, played their first game on January 31, 1877.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Very soon thereafter, those McGill students wrote the first hockey rule book.<sup id="cite_ref-Lennox2009_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lennox2009-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill alumnus <a href="/wiki/James_Naismith" title="James Naismith">James Naismith</a> invented basketball in early December 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Herman_Smith-Johannsen" title="Herman Smith-Johannsen">Herman &quot;Jackrabbit&quot; Smith-Johannsen</a> popularized cross-country skiing in North America from McGill's Gault Estate in Mont St. Hilaire. Johannsen also helped coach Canada's 1932 Olympic team.</p> 
     <p>There has been a McGill alumnus or alumna competing at every <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> Swimmer <a href="/wiki/George_Hodgson" title="George Hodgson">George Hodgson</a> won two gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/1912_Summer_Olympics" title="1912 Summer Olympics">1912 Summer Olympics</a>, ice hockey goaltender <a href="/wiki/Kim_St-Pierre" title="Kim St-Pierre">Kim St-Pierre</a> won gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a> and at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a>. Other 2006 gold medalists are <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Heil" title="Jennifer Heil">Jennifer Heil</a> (women's freestyle mogul) and goaltender <a href="/wiki/Charline_Labont%C3%A9" title="Charline Labont&eacute;">Charline Labont&eacute;</a> (women's ice hockey).</p> 
     <p>In 1996, the McGill Sports <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" title="Hall of Fame" class="mw-redirect">Hall of Fame</a> was established to honour its best student athletes. Notable members of the Hall of Fame include <a href="/wiki/James_Naismith" title="James Naismith">James Naismith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_David_Pierce" title="Sydney David Pierce">Sydney Pierce</a>.</p> 
     <p>A 2005 <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a> scandal forced the cancellation of the final two games in the McGill Redmen football season. In 2006, McGill's Senate approved a proposed anti-hazing policy to define forbidden initiation practices.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p><i>The McGill University song book,</i> compiled by a committee of graduates and undergraduates, was published in Montreal by W.F. Brown, circa 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>'Alma Mater McGill,' with words by J. McDougall;</li> 
      <li>'L'Enfant du McGill,' with words by Louis-Honor&eacute; Fr&eacute;chette, and music by Guillaume Couture;</li> 
      <li>'God Save McGill,' with words by W.M. Mackeracher, tune 'God Save the Queen';</li> 
      <li>'A Health to Old McGill,' with words by R.W. Huntingdon, and music by Mrs W.C. Baynes;</li> 
      <li>'McGill,' with words by C.W. Colby, sung to the tune 'The Gay Cavalier';</li> 
      <li>'McGill Revisited,' with words by John Cox,</li> 
      <li>'McGill Students' with words by W.N. Evans;</li> 
      <li>'The Student of McGill,' with words by R.D. McGibbon<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" style=""> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"> 
         <div style="width: 52px;">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" /></a>
         </div> </td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style=""><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references or sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help improve this section by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.      </table> 
     <p>McGill maintains an academic and athletic rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>. Animosity between rowing athletes<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> at the two schools has inspired an annual boat race between the two universities in the spring of each year since 1997, inspired by the famous <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">Oxford-Cambridge Boat Race</a>. The football rivalry, which started in 1884, ended after Canadian university athletic divisions were re-organized in 2000; the Ontario-Quebec Intercollegiate Football Conference was divided into <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Student_Sports_Federation" title="Quebec Student Sports Federation" class="mw-redirect">Quebec Student Sports Federation</a>. The rivalry returned in 2002 when it transferred to the annual home-and-home hockey games between the two institutions. Queen's students refer to these matches as &quot;Kill McGill&quot; games, and usually show up in Montreal in atypically large numbers to cheer on the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Golden_Gaels" title="Queen's Golden Gaels">Queen's Golden Gaels</a> hockey team. In 2007, McGill students arrived in bus-loads to cheer on the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Redmen" title="McGill Redmen">McGill Redmen</a>, occupying a third of Queen's Jock Harty Arena.</p> 
     <p>The school also competes in the annual &quot;<a href="/wiki/Old_Four" title="Old Four">Old Four (IV)</a>&quot; soccer tournament, with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario" title="University of Western Ontario">University of Western Ontario</a>.</p> 
     <p>McGill and <a href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard" class="mw-redirect">Harvard</a> are also athletic rivals, as demonstrated by the biennial Harvard-McGill rugby games, alternately played in Montreal and Cambridge.</p> 
     <p>In an episode of <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a>, Marge described McGill as the &quot;Harvard of Canada&quot; to which Lisa responded, &quot;Anything that's the 'something' of the 'something' isn't really the 'anything' of 'anything'.&quot; In addition, a popular student t-shirt sold at McGill spoofs this by displaying &quot;Harvard - America's McGill&quot;.</p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McGill_in_fiction">McGill in fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: McGill in fiction">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In fiction, characters from movies and television shows have also been portrayed as McGill students, professors, or researchers. Fictional alumni from McGill include Lieutenant Alan McGregor, played by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cooper" title="Gary Cooper">Gary Cooper</a> in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lives_of_a_Bengal_Lancer" title="The Lives of a Bengal Lancer">Lives Of the Bengal Lancers</a></i> (1935), and Major Donald Craig, a Canadian commando serving with British special forces during World War II, portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Rock_Hudson" title="Rock Hudson">Rock Hudson</a> in the 1967 war movie <i><a href="/wiki/Tobruk_(1967_film)" title="Tobruk (1967 film)">Tobruk</a></i> (though the film was loosely based on real events, it is not clear whether or not Hudson's character was based on a real person: most likely he was a <a href="/wiki/Pastiche" title="Pastiche">pastiche</a> character, given a Canadian background as cover for Hudson's inability to emulate a British accent). In the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Network" title="Fox Network" class="mw-redirect">Fox Network</a> television drama <i><a href="/wiki/House_(TV_series)" title="House (TV series)">House</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/James_Wilson_(House)" title="James Wilson (House)">James Wilson</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Oncologist" title="Oncologist" class="mw-redirect">oncologist</a> at the Princeton-Plainsboro Teaching Hospital is also a McGill alumnus. On the animated sitcom <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a>, the school was referenced by Marge as &quot;The <a href="/wiki/Harvard" title="Harvard" class="mw-redirect">Harvard</a> of Canada.&quot; <a href="/wiki/Sasquatch_(comics)" title="Sasquatch (comics)">Walter Langkowski</a>, a researcher from the Marvel Comics Canadian superhero series <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Flight" title="Alpha Flight">Alpha Flight</a>, is portrayed as a McGill-based <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">biophysicist</a> researching the <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">gamma radiation</a> accident which created <a href="/wiki/Hulk_(comics)" title="Hulk (comics)">the Hulk</a>. Langkowski's discoveries transformed him into the <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">superhero</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Sasquatch_(comics)" title="Sasquatch (comics)">Sasquatch</a>. McGill is also referenced in several of <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Reichs" title="Kathy Reichs">Kathy Reichs</a>' Temperance Brennan novels. In Robert Ludlum's novel <a href="/wiki/The_Bourne_Identity_(novel)" title="The Bourne Identity (novel)">The Bourne Identity</a> the main female protagonist, Marie St. Jacques, is a McGill graduate. In the 2010 Canadian horror film <a href="/wiki/Altitude_(film)" title="Altitude (film)">Altitude</a> the protagonist Sara was due to be an incoming freshman at McGill.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_links">Historical links</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Historical links">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, one of four <a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">ancient Scottish universities</a> and member of the British <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>. Founded in 1451, the original benefactor of McGill College, James McGill, studied here in the 1750s<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> before his family worked as merchants in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> The two universities continue this link today as part of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international student exchange programme.</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>, one of four <a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">ancient Scottish universities</a> and member of the British <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>. The University was founded as a civic institution in 1583 and has maintained a strong reputation in the study of medicine, among other disciplines. McGill's first (and, for several years, its only) faculty, Medicine, was founded by four physicians/surgeons who had trained in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> In common with Glasgow, Edinburgh shares an international exchange link with McGill through <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>As a public university, McGill is not as dependent on its endowment for operating revenue as some of its international peers. The McGill endowment only provides approximately 10 per cent of the school's annual operating revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Nonetheless, McGill's endowment rests within the top 10 percent of all North American post-secondary institutions' endowments.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> While McGill's conservative investment policy has protected it from the more substantial losses experienced at many other universities during the market crisis of 2008–2009, it still faced a 20% endowment decline from approximately $920 million to $740 million.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Valued at $21,633 per student, the university maintains one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_universities_by_endowment" title="List of Canadian universities by endowment">largest endowments among Canadian universities</a> on a per-student basis.</p> 
     <p>In an open letter to faculty and students, Heather Munroe-Blum wrote: &quot;The next few years do not promise to be easy. But in facing this challenge, McGill has a unique advantage in addition to that of the fundamental progress we have made. This university has lived with restricted resources and uncertainty for almost two hundred years – it is part of our culture. And yet, against this backdrop of hardship, we have always retained our commitment to excellence. We are one of the world’s great universities. This will not change. In my installation speech in the spring of 2003, I said McGill &quot;punches above its weight.&quot; We will continue to do so. In order to stay the course, we must now move with confidence, pride, excitement and discipline to seize every opportunity to put McGill in an ideal position to leap forward with the inevitable recovery.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_McGill">Campaign McGill</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Campaign McGill">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i>Campaign McGill: History in the Making</i> is a five-year comprehensive campaign that began in October 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> with the goal of raising over $750 million for the purpose of further &quot;attracting and retaining top talent in Quebec, to increase access to quality education and to further enhance McGill's ability to address critical global problems.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest goal of any Canadian university fundraising campaign in history,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> within the first six months, McGill had accumulated over $400 million towards its efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> Support to McGill’s annual fund has actually increased during the market crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_190-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Principal Heather Munroe-Blum, she is confident that Campaign McGill will reach its $750 million goal by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_190-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On June 18, 2013 Principal Heather Munroe-Blum officially closed the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Globe_and_Mail_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Globe_and_Mail-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> The university surpassed its initial goal of $750 million and raised more than $1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Montreal_Gazette_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montreal_Gazette-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition">Tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tuition">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tuition" title="Tuition" class="mw-redirect">Tuition fees</a> vary significantly between in-<a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">province</a>, out-of-province, and international students, with full-time Quebec students paying around $2,167.80<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> per year, Canadian students from other provinces paying around $5,858.10<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> per year, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_nationality_law" title="Canadian nationality law">international</a> students paying $14,461.80–$24,840 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> Students must also pay housing costs, though Montreal has some of the least expensive housing among large North American cities.</p> 
     <p>Since 1996, McGill, in accordance with the Minist&egrave;re de l'&Eacute;ducation, du Loisir et du Sport (MELS), has had eight categories that qualifies certain international students to be excused from paying international fees. These categories include: students from France, a quota of students from select countries which have agreements with MELS, which include <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, China, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> students holding diplomatic status, including their <a href="/wiki/Dependent_(law)" title="Dependent (law)" class="mw-redirect">dependents</a>, and students enrolled in certain language programs leading to a degree in French.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the school year 2008-2009, McGill's graduate business program became funded by tuition, and was the last business school in Canada to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholarships_and_financial_aid">Scholarships and financial aid</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Scholarships and financial aid">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Scholarships" title="Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Scholarships</a> at McGill are relatively difficult to attain, compared to other Canadian universities.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> This is predominantly due to the number of high academic achievers at the school. For out-of-province first year undergraduate students, a high school average of 95% is required to receive a guaranteed one-year entrance scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-Entrance_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entrance-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> To be considered for the same scholarships, Quebec CEGEP students need a minimum r-score of 35.5, United States high school students need a minimum A average as well as at least 700 in each SAT or 33 in the ACT, and French Baccalaureate students need an average of 15.5 plus a minimum score of 14 in each course; similarly, students in the British education system need As in both GCSE Level and predicted Advanced Level results, and International Baccalaureate students need to attain a minimum overall average of 6.9 on predicted grades or a score of 42 on exam results. In general, entrance scholarship recipients rank in the top 1–2% of their class.</p> 
     <p>For renewal of previously earned scholarships, students generally need to be within the top 10% of their faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> For in-course scholarships in particular, students must be within the top 5% of their faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-incoursescholarships_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incoursescholarships-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deanshonourlist_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deanshonourlist-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> McGill itself outlines scholarship considerations as follows: &quot;Competition for basic and major scholarships is intense at McGill. An extraordinary number of exceptional applications are received each year and therefore we cannot award scholarships to all good candidates.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Entrance_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entrance-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has joined Project Hero, a scholarship program cofounded by General (Ret'd) <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hillier" title="Rick Hillier">Rick Hillier</a> for the families of fallen <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_McGill_University_people" title="List of McGill University people">List of McGill University people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg/170px-Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg/255px-Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg/340px-Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ernest_Rutherford2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> As chair of physics at McGill, 
        <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> was awarded the Nobel Prize in Chemistry in 1908 for his work in atomic physics.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the arts, McGill students include three <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Templeton_Prize" title="Templeton Prize">Templeton Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(philosopher)" title="Charles Taylor (philosopher)">Charles Taylor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> essayist and novelist <a href="/wiki/John_Ralston_Saul" title="John Ralston Saul">John Ralston Saul</a>, a Companion of the Order of Canada along with Charles Taylor, <a href="/wiki/Juno_Award" title="Juno Award">Juno Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Sam_Roberts" title="Sam Roberts">Sam Roberts</a>, Singer-Songwriter Prita Chhabra and <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a>, best known for his portrayal of <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">Captain Kirk</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a></i> and winner of several <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Awards" title="Emmy Awards" class="mw-redirect">Emmy Awards</a>. Nine <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners studied at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i> charting musician and vocalist <a href="/wiki/Mary_Fahl" title="Mary Fahl">Mary Fahl</a> also attended McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-electricreview_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-electricreview-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Win_Butler" title="Win Butler">Win Butler</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9gine_Chassagne" title="R&eacute;gine Chassagne">R&eacute;gine Chassagne</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning group <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a> also met while studying at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> Musician and visual artist <a href="/wiki/Claire_Boucher" title="Claire Boucher" class="mw-redirect">Claire Boucher</a>, better known under the moniker Grimes, also attended McGill before dropping out.</p> 
     <p>In the sciences, students include doctors, inventors, three astronauts and scientist <a href="/wiki/Dr._Mark_J._Poznansky" title="Dr. Mark J. Poznansky" class="mw-redirect">Dr. Mark J. Poznansky</a>, a member of the Order of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 16, 2009, the 42nd American president, Bill Clinton accepted an Honorary Doctorate from McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Taylor_(philosopher).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg/170px-Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg" width="170" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg/255px-Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg/340px-Charles_Taylor_%28philosopher%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Taylor_(philosopher).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(philosopher)" title="Charles Taylor (philosopher)">Charles Taylor</a> studied at the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a> as a Rhodes Scholar from McGill.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Some politicians and government officials both within Canada and abroad are McGill alumni, including two <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Canadian prime ministers</a> and eleven justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>. Progressive Conservative MP <a href="/wiki/Robert_Layton" title="Robert Layton">Robert Layton</a> and his son, <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_of_Canada" title="New Democratic Party of Canada" class="mw-redirect">New Democratic Party</a> leader and <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Canada)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Canada)" class="mw-redirect">Leader of the Opposition</a> <a href="/wiki/Jack_Layton" title="Jack Layton">Jack Layton</a>, also attended McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vaira_V%C4%AB%C4%B7e-Freiberga" title="Vaira Vīķe-Freiberga">Vaira Vīķe-Freiberga</a> completed her Ph.D. at McGill and was elected as president of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Latvia" title="Republic of Latvia" class="mw-redirect">Republic of Latvia</a> in 1999 as the first female president in Eastern Europe after Turkey's <a href="/wiki/Tansu_%C3%87iller" title="Tansu &Ccedil;iller">Tansu &Ccedil;iller</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Nazif" title="Ahmed Nazif">Ahmed Nazif</a> also completed a Ph.D. at McGill in 1983 and has served as the youngest <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> since the republic's founding 1953. In the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federal_election,_2011" title="Canadian federal election, 2011">2011 Canadian election</a>, five McGill students—undergraduates <a href="/wiki/Charmaine_Borg" title="Charmaine Borg">Charmaine Borg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Dub%C3%A9" title="Matthew Dub&eacute;">Matthew Dub&eacute;</a>, <a href="/wiki/Myl%C3%A8ne_Freeman" title="Myl&egrave;ne Freeman">Myl&egrave;ne Freeman</a> (graduating shortly after the election) and <a href="/wiki/Laurin_Liu" title="Laurin Liu">Laurin Liu</a> plus graduate student <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Nicholls" title="Jamie Nicholls">Jamie Nicholls</a>—were elected as NDP MPs.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, 2006 McGill graduate <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Sheyman" title="Ilya Sheyman" class="mw-redirect">Ilya Sheyman</a> is a Democratic candidate for the <a href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" title="U.S. House of Representatives" class="mw-redirect">U.S. House of Representatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Corporate leaders and <a href="/wiki/Media_personalities" title="Media personalities" class="mw-redirect">media personalities</a> have also studied at McGill. Leading Canadian philanthropist and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Schulich" title="Seymour Schulich">Seymour Schulich</a> donated $20 million, the highest donation to any music school in Canada, to the newly-named <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Music" title="Schulich School of Music">Schulich School of Music</a>. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Mintzberg" title="Henry Mintzberg">Henry Mintzberg</a>, a professor at McGill's <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a> is an acclaimed management thinker and contributes to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>. Mintzberg is an Officer of the Order of Canada. Co-founder and president of <a href="/wiki/Matrox" title="Matrox">Matrox Electronic Systems Ltd.</a>, which innovates globally in graphics, video editing, and image processing, <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Trottier" title="Lorne Trottier">Lorne Trottier</a> has donated $10 million towards services in information and technology at McGill. The new engineering building is called Trottier, named after Lorne Trottier. <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Black" title="Conrad Black">Conrad Black</a>, a major media magnate and convicted fraudster, also studied at McGill.</p> 
     <p>McGill students are also recognized as athletes, including various members of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Team_(disambiguation)" title="Canadian National Team (disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect">Canadian national teams</a> and twenty-eight <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medalists. Since the Olympics began, McGill has produced 112 Olympians who have won a total of eight gold medals, nine silver, and eleven bronze.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Viner" title="Jacob Viner">Jacob Viner</a>, who would later go on to form the beginnings of the modern day <a href="/wiki/Chicago_School_of_Economics" title="Chicago School of Economics" class="mw-redirect">Chicago School of Economics</a>, earned his undergraduate degree from McGill. <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins School of Medicine</a>, and the originator of the concept of <a href="/wiki/Residency_(medicine)" title="Residency (medicine)">medical residency</a>, received his medical degree from McGill.</p> 
     <p>Professors at McGill have won 26 <a href="/wiki/Prix_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Prix du Qu&eacute;bec">Prix du Qu&eacute;bec</a>, 14 Prix de l'<a href="/wiki/Association_francophone_pour_le_savoir" title="Association francophone pour le savoir">Association francophone pour le savoir</a> and 21 <a href="/wiki/Isaak-Walton-Killam_Award" title="Isaak-Walton-Killam Award" class="mw-redirect">Killam Prizes</a>. Twelve <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureates" title="Nobel Laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Laureates</a> have studied or taught at McGill.</p> 
     <p>Since 1902, Canadian undergraduate students have been eligible for Rhodes Scholarships to study at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>. More than any other university, McGill students have won 132 Rhodes Scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-rhodes_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> These students include parliamentary and cabinet ministers <a href="/wiki/David_Lewis_(politician)" title="David Lewis (politician)">David Lewis</a> (1932), <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Gillespie" title="Alastair Gillespie">Alastair Gillespie</a> (1947), and <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Mass%C3%A9" title="Marcel Mass&eacute;">Marcel Mass&eacute;</a> (1963), the political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(philosopher)" title="Charles Taylor (philosopher)">Charles Taylor</a> (1952), and the U.S. political advisor and inventor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_Phillips_(inventor)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jack Phillips (inventor) (page does not exist)">Jack Phillips</a> (1978).</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="noprint tright portal" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;">
